-<ul class="simple">

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>aggregate</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/aggregate/">aggregate</a> plugin.
-This plugin requires extra setup, specifically, a cron job. See the
-plugin&#39;s documentation for details.</p>
-
-<p>This directive allows content from other feeds to be aggregated into the wiki.
-Aggregate a feed as follows:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!aggregate  name=&quot;example blog&quot; dir=&quot;example&quot;
-feedurl=&quot;http://example.com/index.rss&quot;
-url=&quot;http://example.com/&quot; updateinterval=&quot;15&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>That example aggregates posts from the specified RSS feed, updating no
-more frequently than once every 15 minutes (though possibly less
-frequently, if the cron job runs less frequently than that), and puts a
-page per post under the example/ directory in the wiki.</p>
-
-<p>You can then use ikiwiki&#39;s <a href="../inline/">inline</a> directive to create a blog of one or
-more aggregated feeds. For example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!inline  pages=&quot;internal(example/*)&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Note the use of <code>internal()</code> in the <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> to match
-aggregated pages. By default, aggregated pages are internal pages,
-which prevents them from showing up directly in the wiki, and so this
-special <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> is needed to match them.</p>
-
-<h2>usage</h2>
-
-<p>Here are descriptions of all the supported parameters to the <code>aggregate</code>
-directive:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>name</code> - A name for the feed. Each feed must have a unique name.
-Required.</li>
-<li><code>url</code> - The url to the web page for the feed that&#39;s being aggregated.
-Required.</li>
-<li><code>dir</code> - The directory in the wiki where pages should be saved. Optional,
-if not specified, the directory is based on the name of the feed.</li>
-<li><code>feedurl</code> - The url to the feed. Optional, if it&#39;s not specified ikiwiki
-will look for feeds on the <code>url</code>. RSS and atom feeds are supported.</li>
-<li><code>updateinterval</code> - How often to check for new posts, in minutes. Default
-is 15 minutes.</li>
-<li><code>expireage</code> - Expire old items from this feed if they are older than
-a specified number of days. Default is to never expire on age.</li>
-<li><code>expirecount</code> - Expire old items from this feed if there are more than
-the specified number total. Oldest items will be expired first. Default
-is to never expire on count.</li>
-<li><code>tag</code> - A tag to tag each post from the feed with. A good tag to use is
-the name of the feed. Can be repeated multiple times. The <a href="../tag/">tag</a> plugin
-must be enabled for this to work.</li>
-<li><code>template</code> - Template to use for creating the aggregated pages. Defaults to
-aggregatepost.</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>Note that even if you are using subversion or another revision control
-system, pages created by aggregation will <em>not</em> be checked into revision
-control.</p>
-
-</section>

-<p>The <code>brokenlinks</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/brokenlinks/">brokenlinks</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive generates a list of broken links on pages in the wiki. This is
-a useful way to find pages that still need to be written, or links that
-are written wrong.</p>
-
-<p>The optional parameter &quot;pages&quot; can be a <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> specifying the
-pages to search for broken links, default is search them all.</p>
-
-<p>Example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!brokenlinks  pages=&quot;* and !recentchanges&quot;]]
-</code></pre>

@@ -1,162 +0,0 @@

-<link rel="icon" href="../../../favicon.ico" type="image/x-icon" />

-<article class="page">

-<section class="pageheader">
-<header class="header">
-<span>

-<span class="title">

-</span>
-</span>
-
-
-<form method="get" action="http://www.google.com/search" id="searchform">
- <div>
-  <input name="sitesearch" value="http://weakish.github.com/" type="hidden" />
-  <input name="q" value="" id="searchbox" size="16" maxlength="255" type="text"

-<div id="pagebody">
-
-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>calendar</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/calendar/">calendar</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive displays a calendar, similar to the typical calendars shown on
-some blogs.</p>
-
-<h1>examples</h1>
-
-<pre><code>[[!calendar  ]]
-
-[[!calendar  type=&quot;month&quot; pages=&quot;blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot;]]
-
-[[!calendar  type=&quot;year&quot; year=&quot;2005&quot; pages=&quot;blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<h2>setup</h2>
-
-<p>The calendar is essentially a fancy front end to archives of previous
-pages, usually used for blogs. It can produce a calendar for a given month,
-or a list of months for a given year. The month format calendar simply
-links to any page posted on each day of the month. The year format calendar
-links to archive pages, with names like <code>archives/2007</code> (for all of 2007)
-and <code>archives/2007/01</code> (for January, 2007).</p>
-
-<p>While you can insert calendar directives anywhere on your wiki, including
-in the sidebar, you&#39;ll also need to create these archive pages. They
-typically use this directive to display a calendar, and also use <a href="../inline/">inline</a>
-to display or list pages created in the given time frame.</p>
-
-<p>The <code>ikiwiki-calendar</code> command can be used to automatically generate the
-archive pages. It also refreshes the wiki, updating the calendars to
-highlight the current day. This command is typically run at midnight from
-cron.</p>
-
-<p>An example crontab:</p>
-
-<pre><code>0 0 * * * ikiwiki-calendar ~/ikiwiki.setup &quot;posts/* and !*/Discussion&quot;
-</code></pre>
-
-<h2>usage</h2>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>type</code> - Used to specify the type of calendar wanted. Can be one of
-&quot;month&quot; or &quot;year&quot;. The default is a month view calendar.</li>
-<li><code>pages</code> - Specifies the <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> of pages to link to from the
-month calendar. Defaults to &quot;*&quot;.</li>
-<li><code>archivebase</code> - Configures the base of the archives hierarchy. 
-The default is &quot;archives&quot;. Note that this default can also be overridden
-for the whole wiki by setting <code>archivebase</code> in ikiwiki&#39;s setup file.
-Calendars link to pages under here, with names like &quot;2010/04&quot; and
-&quot;2010&quot;. These pages can be automatically created using the
-<code>ikiwiki-calendar</code> program. </li>
-<li><code>year</code> - The year for which the calendar is requested. Defaults to the
-current year. Can also use -1 to refer to last year, and so on.</li>
-<li><code>month</code> - The numeric month for which the calendar is requested, in the
-range 1..12. Used only for the month view calendar, and defaults to the
-current month. Can also use -1 to refer to last month, and so on.</li>
-<li><code>week_start_day</code> - A number, in the range 0..6, which represents the day
-of the week that the month calendar starts with. 0 is Sunday, 1 is Monday,
-and so on. Defaults to 0, which is Sunday.</li>
-<li><code>months_per_row</code> - In the year calendar, number of months to place in
-each row. Defaults to 3.</li>
-</ul>
-
-</section>

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>color</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/color/">color</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive can be used to color a piece of text on a page.
-It can be used to set the foreground and/or background color of the text.</p>
-
-<p>You can use a color name (e.g. <code>white</code>) or HTML code (e.g. <code>#ffffff</code>)
-to define colors. </p>
-
-<h2>examples</h2>
-
-<p>Here the foreground color is defined as a word, while the background color
-is defined as a HTML color code:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!color  foreground=white background=#ff0000 text=&quot;White text on red background&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The background color is missing, so the text is displayed on default
-background:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!color  foreground=white text=&quot;White text on default color background&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The foreground is missing, so the text has the default foreground color:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!color  background=#ff0000 text=&quot;Default color text on red background&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-</section>

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>comment</code> directive is supplied by the
-<a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/comments/">comments</a> plugin, and is used to add a comment
-to a page. Typically, the directive is the only thing on a comment page,
-and is filled out by the comment plugin when a user posts a comment.</p>
-
-<p>Example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!comment  format=mdwn
-username=&quot;foo&quot;
-subject=&quot;Bar&quot;
-date=&quot;2009-06-02T19:05:01Z&quot;
-content=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-Blah blah.
-&quot;&quot;&quot;
-]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<h2>usage</h2>
-
-<p>The only required parameter is <code>content</code>, the others just add or override
-metadata of the comment.</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>content</code> - Text to display for the comment.
-Note that <a href="../">directives</a>
-may not be allowed, depending on the configuration
-of the comment plugin.</li>
-<li><code>format</code> - Specifies the markup used for the content.</li>
-<li><code>subject</code> - Subject for the comment.</li>
-<li><code>date</code> - Date the comment was posted. Can be entered in
-nearly any format, since it&#39;s parsed by <a href="http://search.cpan.org/search?mode=dist&amp;query=TimeDate">TimeDate</a></li>
-<li><code>username</code> - Used to record the username (or OpenID)
-of a logged in commenter.</li>
-<li><code>nickname</code> - Name to display for a logged in commenter.
-(Optional; used for OpenIDs.)</li>
-<li><code>ip</code> - Can be used to record the IP address of a commenter,
-if they posted anonymously.</li>
-<li><code>claimedauthor</code> - Records the name that the user entered,
-if anonymous commenters are allowed to enter their (unverified)
-name.</li>
-</ul>
-
-</section>
-
-

-  <input name="q" value="" id="searchbox" size="16" maxlength="255" type="text"

-<div id="pagebody">
-
-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>copy</code>, <code>cut</code> and <code>paste</code> directives are supplied by the
-<a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/cutpaste/">cutpaste</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>With these directives you can store and recall pieces of text in a page:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>[[!cut  id=name text=&quot;text&quot;]]</code> memorizes the text allowing to recall it
-using the given ID.  The text being cut is not included in the output.</li>
-<li><code>[[!copy  id=name text=&quot;text&quot;]]</code> memorizes the text allowing to recall it
-using the given ID.  The text being cut <em>is</em> included in the output.</li>
-<li><code>[[!paste  id=name]]</code> is replaced by the previously memorized text.</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>The text being cut, copied and pasted can freely include wiki markup, including
-more calls to cut, copy and paste.</p>
-
-<p>You do not need to memorize the text before using it: a cut directive can
-follow the paste directive that uses its text.  In fact, this is quite useful
-to postpone big blocks of text like long annotations and have a more natural
-flow.  For example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!toggleable  id=&quot;cut&quot; text=&quot;[[!paste id=cutlongdesc]]&quot;]]
-[[!toggleable  id=&quot;copy&quot; text=&quot;[[!paste id=copylongdesc]]&quot;]]
-[[!toggleable  id=&quot;paste&quot; text=&quot;[[!paste id=pastelongdesc]]&quot;]]
-
-[...some time later...]
-
-[[!cut  id=cutlongdesc text=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-   blah blah blah
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-[[!cut  id=copylongdesc text=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-   blah blah blah
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-[[!cut  id=pastelongdesc text=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-   blah blah blah
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>This can potentially be used to create loops, but ikiwiki is clever and breaks
-them.</p>
-
-<p>Since you can paste without using double quotes, copy and paste can be used to
-nest directives that require multiline parameters inside each other:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!toggleable  id=foo text=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-  [[!toggleable id=bar text=&quot;[[!paste id=baz]]&quot;]]
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-
-[[!cut  id=baz text=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-multiline parameter!
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-
-</div>
-

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>date</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/date/">date</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive can be used to display a date on a page, using the same
-display method that is used to display the modification date in the page
-footer, and other dates in the wiki. This can be useful for consistency
-of display, or if you want to embed parseable dates into the page source.</p>
-
-<p>Like the dates used by the <a href="../meta/">meta</a> directive, the date can be entered in
-nearly any format, since it&#39;s parsed by <a href="http://search.cpan.org/search?mode=dist&amp;query=TimeDate">TimeDate</a>.</p>
-
-<p>For example, an update to a page with an embedded date stamp could look
-like:</p>
-
-<pre><code>Updated [[!date  &quot;Wed, 25 Nov 2009 01:11:55 -0500&quot;]]: mumble mumble
-</code></pre>
-
-</section>

-<p>The <code>edittemplate</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/edittemplate/">edittemplate</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive allows registering template pages, that provide default
-content for new pages created using the web frontend. To register a
-template, insert a <a href="../template/">template</a> directive on some other page.</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!edittemplate  template=&quot;bugtemplate&quot; match=&quot;bugs/*&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>In the above example, the page named &quot;bugtemplate&quot; is registered as a
-template to be used when any page named &quot;bugs/*&quot; is created. To avoid
-the directive displaying a note about the template being registered, add
-&quot;silent=yes&quot;.</p>
-
-<p>Often the template page contains a simple skeleton for a particular type of
-page. For the bug report pages in the above example, it might look
-something like:</p>
-
-<pre><code>Package: 
-Version: 
-Reproducible: y/n
-Details:
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The template page can also contain <a href="http://search.cpan.org/search?mode=dist&amp;query=HTML%3A%3ATemplate">HTML::Template</a> directives,
-like other ikiwiki <a href="../../../templates/">templates</a>. Currently only one variable is
-set: <code>&lt;TMPL_VAR name&gt;</code> is replaced with the name of the page being
-created.</p>
-
-<hr />
-
-<p>It&#39;s generally not a good idea to put the <code>edittemplate</code> directive in
-the template page itself, since the directive would then be included as
-part of the template on new pages, which would then in turn be registered
-as templates. If multiple pages are registered as templates for a new page,
-an arbitrary one is chosen, so that could get confusing.</p>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-
-</div>

-plugin.</p>
-
-<p>The directive allows formatting a chunk of text using any available page
-format. It takes two parameters. First is the type of format to use,
-ie the extension that would be used for a standalone file of this type.
-Second is the text to format.</p>

-some other format:</p>

-    2
-bar
-    3
-    4
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Note that if the highlight plugin is enabled, this directive can also be
-used to display syntax highlighted code. Many languages and formats are
-supported. For example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!format  perl &quot;&quot;&quot;
-print &quot;hello, world\n&quot;;
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>

-<p>The <code>graph</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/graphviz/">graphviz</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive allows embedding <a href="http://www.graphviz.org/">graphviz</a> graphs in a
-page.  Example usage:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!graph  src=&quot;a -&gt; b -&gt; c; a -&gt; c;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Note that graphs will only show up in previews if your browser has
-<a href="https://secure.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/wiki/data%3A%20URI">data: URI</a> support, or if the same graph already exists on that
-page.</p>
-
-<p>The <code>graph</code> directive supports the following parameters:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>src</code> - The graphviz source to render.</li>
-<li><code>type</code> - The type of graph to render: <code>graph</code> or <code>digraph</code>.  Defaults to
-<code>digraph</code>.</li>
-<li><code>prog</code> - The graphviz program to render with: <code>dot</code>, <code>neato</code>, <code>fdp</code>, <code>twopi</code>,
-or <code>circo</code>.  Defaults to <code>dot</code>.</li>
-<li><code>height</code>, <code>width</code> - Limit the size of the graph to a given height and width,
-in inches. You must specify both to limit the size; otherwise, graphviz will
-choose a size, without any limit.</li>
-</ul>
-
-</section>

-
-<p>This directive allows inserting a randomly generated haiku into a wiki page.
-Just type:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!haiku  hint=&quot;argument&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>[[!haiku  hint=&quot;argument test&quot;]]</p>
-
-<p>The hint parameter can be omitted, it only provides the generator a hint of
-what to write the haiku about. If no hint is given, it might base it on the
-page name. Since the vocabulary it knows is very small, many hints won&#39;t
-affect the result at all.</p>

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>if</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/conditional/">conditional</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>With this directive, you can make text be conditionally displayed on a page.
-For example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!if  test=&quot;enabled(smiley)&quot;
-      then=&quot;The smiley plugin is enabled :-)&quot;
-      else=&quot;No smiley plugin here..&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>If the specified <code>test</code> succeeds, the <code>then</code> text will be displayed,
-otherwise the <code>else</code> text will be displayed. The <code>else</code> part is optional.</p>
-
-<p>The <code>then</code> and <code>else</code> values can include any markup that would be allowed
-in the wiki page outside the template. Triple-quoting the values even allows
-quotes to be included.</p>
-
-<p>The <code>test</code> is a <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a>; if it matches any page in the wiki
-then it succeeds. So you can do things like testing for the existence of a
-page or pages, testing to see if any pages were created in a given month,
-and so on.</p>
-
-<p>If you want the <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> to only match against the page that
-contains the conditional, rather than matching against all pages in the
-wiki, set the &quot;all&quot; parameter to &quot;no&quot;.</p>
-
-<p>In an <code>if</code> directive, the regular <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> syntax is expanded
-with the following additional tests:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><p>enabled(plugin)</p>
-
-<p>Tests whether the specified plugin is enabled.</p></li>
-<li><p>sourcepage(glob)</p>
-
-<p>Tests whether the glob matches the name of the page that contains the
-conditional.</p></li>
-<li><p>destpage(glob)</p>
-
-<p>Tests whether the glob matches the name of the page that is being built.
-That might be different than the name of the page that contains the
-conditional, if it&#39;s being inlined into another page.</p></li>
-<li><p>included()</p>
-
-<p>Tests whether the page is being included onto another page, for example
-via <a href="../inline/">inline</a> or <a href="../map/">map</a>.  Note that pages inserted into other pages
-via <a href="../template/">template</a> are not matched here.</p></li>
-</ul>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-
-</div>

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>img</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/img/">img</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This is an image handling directive.  While ikiwiki supports inlining full-size
-images by making a <a href="../../wikilink/">WikiLink</a> that points to the image, using
-this directive you can easily scale down an image for inclusion onto a page,
-providing a link to a full-size version.</p>
-
-<h2>usage</h2>
-
-<pre><code>[[!img  image1.jpg size=&quot;200x200&quot; alt=&quot;clouds&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The image file will be searched for using the same rules as used to find
-the file pointed to by a <a href="../../wikilink/">WikiLink</a>.</p>
-
-<p>The <code>size</code> parameter is optional, defaulting to full size. Note that the
-original image&#39;s aspect ratio is always preserved, even if this means
-making the image smaller than the specified size. You can also specify only
-the width or the height, and the other value will be calculated based on
-it: &quot;200x&quot;, &quot;x200&quot;</p>
-
-<p>You can also pass <code>alt</code>, <code>title</code>, <code>class</code>, <code>align</code>, <code>id</code>, <code>hspace</code>, and
-<code>vspace</code> parameters.
-These are passed through unchanged to the html img tag. If you include a
-<code>caption</code> parameter, the caption will be displayed centered beneath the image.</p>
-
-<p>The <code>link</code> parameter is used to control whether the scaled image links
-to the full size version. By default it does; set &quot;link=somepage&quot; to link
-to another page instead, or &quot;link=no&quot; to disable the link, or
-&quot;link=http://url&quot; to link to a given url.</p>
-
-<p>You can also set default values that will be applied to all later images on
-the page, unless overridden. Useful when including many images on a page.</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!img  defaults size=200x200 alt=&quot;wedding photo&quot;]]
-[[!img  photo1.jpg]]
-[[!img  photo2.jpg]]
-[[!img  photo3.jpg size=200x600]]
-</code></pre>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-
-</div>

-<div id="pagebody">
-
-<section id="content">
-<p>Directives are similar to a <a href="../wikilink/">WikiLink</a> in form, except they
-begin with <code>!</code> and may contain parameters. The general form is:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!directive  param=&#34;value&#34; param=&#34;value&#34;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>This gets expanded before the rest of the page is processed, and can be used
-to transform the page in various ways.</p>
-
-<p>The quotes around values can be omitted if the value is a simple word.
-Also, some directives may use parameters without values, for example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!tag  foo]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>A directive does not need to all be on one line, it can be
-wrapped to multiple lines if you like:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!directive  foo=&#34;baldersnatch&#34;
-bar=&#34;supercalifragilisticexpialidocious&#34; baz=11]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Also, multiple lines of <em>quoted</em> text can be used for a value.
-To allow quote marks inside the quoted text, delimit the block
-of text with triple-quotes:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!directive  text=&#34;&#34;&#34;
-1. &#34;foo&#34;
-2. &#34;bar&#34;
-3. &#34;baz&#34;
-&#34;&#34;&#34;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>ikiwiki also has an older syntax for directives, which requires a space in
-directives to distinguish them from <a href="../wikilink/">wikilinks</a>. This
-syntax has several disadvantages: it requires a space after directives with
-no parameters (such as <code>[[pagecount ]]</code>), and it prohibits spaces in
-<a href="../wikilink/">wikilinks</a>.  ikiwiki now provides the <code>!</code>-prefixed
-syntax shown above as default.  However, ikiwiki still supports wikis using
-the older syntax, if the <code>prefix_directives</code> option is disabled.</p>
-
-<p>Here is a list of currently available directives in this wiki:</p>
-
-<ul class="listdirectives"><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./brokenlinks/">brokenlinks</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./format/">format</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./if/">if</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./inline/">inline</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./linkmap/">linkmap</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./listdirectives/">listdirectives</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./map/">map</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./meta/">meta</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./orphans/">orphans</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./pagestats/">pagestats</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./pagetemplate/">pagetemplate</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./shortcut/">shortcut</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./table/">table</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./tag/">tag</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./taglink/">taglink</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./template/">template</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./teximg/">teximg</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./toc/">toc</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="./version/">version</a></li></ul>
-
-</section>

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>inline</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/inline/">inline</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This is a directive that allows including one wiki page inside another.
-The most common use of inlining is generating blogs and RSS or Atom feeds.</p>
-
-<p>Example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!inline  pages=&quot;blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot; show=&quot;10&quot; rootpage=&quot;blog&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Any pages that match the specified <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> (in the example, any
-<a href="../../subpage/">SubPage</a> of &quot;blog&quot;) will be part of the blog, and the newest 10
-of them will appear in the page. Note that if files that are not pages
-match the <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a>, they will be included in the feed using RSS
-enclosures, which is useful for podcasting.</p>
-
-<p>The optional <code>rootpage</code> parameter tells the wiki that new posts to this
-blog should default to being <a href="../../subpage/">SubPages</a> of &quot;blog&quot;, and enables a
-form at the top of the blog that can be used to add new items.</p>
-
-<p>If you want your blog to have an archive page listing every post ever made
-to it, you can accomplish that like this:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!inline  pages=&quot;blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot; archive=&quot;yes&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>You can even create an automatically generated list of all the pages on the
-wiki, with the most recently added at the top, like this:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!inline  pages=&quot;* and !*/Discussion&quot; archive=&quot;yes&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>If you want to be able to add pages to a given blog feed by tagging them,
-you can do that too. To tag a page, just make it link to a page or pages 
-that represent its tags. Then use the special <code>link()</code> <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> to match
-all pages that have a given tag:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!inline  pages=&quot;link(life)&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Or include some tags and exclude others:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!inline  pages=&quot;link(debian) and !link(social)&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<h2>usage</h2>
-
-<p>There are many parameters you can use with the <code>inline</code>
-directive. These are the commonly used ones:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>pages</code> - A <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> of the pages to inline.</li>
-<li><code>show</code> - Specify the maximum number of matching pages to inline.
-Default is 10, unless archiving, when the default is to show all.
-Set to 0 to show all matching pages.</li>
-<li><code>archive</code> - If set to &quot;yes&quot;, only list page titles and some metadata, not
-full contents.</li>
-<li><code>description</code> - Sets the description of the rss feed if one is generated.
-Defaults to the name of the wiki.</li>
-<li><code>skip</code> - Specify a number of pages to skip displaying. Can be useful
-to produce a feed that only shows archived pages.</li>
-<li><code>postform</code> - Set to &quot;yes&quot; to enable a form to post new pages to a
-blog.</li>
-<li><code>postformtext</code> - Set to specify text that is displayed in a postform.</li>
-<li><code>rootpage</code> - Enables the postform, and allows controling where
-newly posted pages should go, by specifiying the page that
-they should be a <a href="../../subpage/">SubPage</a> of.</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>Here are some less often needed parameters:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>actions</code> - If set to &quot;yes&quot; add links to the bottom of the inlined pages 
-for editing and discussion (if they would be shown at the top of the page
-itself).</li>
-<li><code>rss</code> - controls generation of an rss feed. If the wiki is configured to
-generate rss feeds by default, set to &quot;no&quot; to disable. If the wiki is
-configured to <code>allowrss</code>, set to &quot;yes&quot; to enable.</li>
-<li><code>atom</code> - controls generation of an atom feed. If the wiki is configured to
-generate atom feeds by default, set to &quot;no&quot; to disable. If the wiki is
-configured to <code>allowatom</code>, set to &quot;yes&quot; to enable.</li>
-<li><code>feeds</code> - controls generation of all types of feeds. Set to &quot;no&quot; to
-disable generating any feeds.</li>
-<li><code>emptyfeeds</code> - Set to &quot;no&quot; to disable generation of empty feeds.
-Has no effect if <code>rootpage</code> or <code>postform</code> is set.</li>
-<li><code>id</code> - Set to specify the value of the HTML <code>id</code> attribute for the
-feed links or the post form. Useful if you have multiple forms in the
-same page.</li>
-<li><code>template</code> - Specifies the template to fill out to display each inlined
-page. By default the <code>inlinepage</code> template is used, while
-the <code>archivepage</code> template is used for archives. Set this parameter to
-use some other, custom template, such as the <code>titlepage</code> template that
-only shows post titles or the <code>microblog</code> template, optimised for
-microblogging. Note that you should still set <code>archive=yes</code> if
-your custom template does not include the page content.</li>
-<li><code>raw</code> - Rather than the default behavior of creating a blog,
-if raw is set to &quot;yes&quot;, the page will be included raw, without additional
-markup around it, as if it were a literal part of the source of the 
-inlining page.</li>
-<li><code>sort</code> - Controls how inlined pages are <a href="../../pagespec/sorting/">sorted</a>.
-The default is to sort the newest created pages first.</li>
-<li><code>reverse</code> - If set to &quot;yes&quot;, causes the sort order to be reversed.</li>
-<li><code>feedshow</code> - Specify the maximum number of matching pages to include in
-the rss/atom feeds. The default is the same as the <code>show</code> value above.</li>
-<li><code>feedonly</code> - Only generate the feed, do not display the pages inline on
-the page.</li>
-<li><code>quick</code> - Build archives in quick mode, without reading page contents for
-metadata. This also turns off generation of any feeds.</li>
-<li><code>timeformat</code> - Use this to specify how to display the time or date for pages
-in the blog. The format string is passed to the strftime(3) function.</li>
-<li><code>feedpages</code> - A <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> of inlined pages to include in the rss/atom
-feeds. The default is the same as the <code>pages</code> value above, and only pages
-matched by that value are included, but some of those can be excluded by
-specifying a tighter <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> here.</li>
-<li><code>guid</code> - If a URI is given here (perhaps a UUID prefixed with <code>urn:uuid:</code>),
-the Atom feed will have this as its <code>&lt;id&gt;</code>. The default is to use the URL
-of the page containing the <code>inline</code> directive.</li>
-<li><code>feedfile</code> - Can be used to change the name of the file generated for the
-feed. This is particularly useful if a page contains multiple feeds.
-For example, set &quot;feedfile=feed&quot; to cause it to generate <code>page/feed.atom</code>
-and/or <code>page/feed.rss</code>. This option is not supported if the wiki is
-configured not to use <code>usedirs</code>.</li>
-<li><code>pagenames</code> - If given instead of <code>pages</code>, this is interpreted as a
-space-separated list of links to pages (with the same
-<a href="../../subpage/linkingrules/">LinkingRules</a> as in a <a href="../../wikilink/">WikiLink</a>), and they are inlined
-in exactly the order given: the <code>sort</code> and <code>pages</code> parameters cannot be used
-in conjunction with this one.</li>
-</ul>
-
-</section>
-
-

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>linkmap</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/linkmap/">linkmap</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive uses <a href="http://www.graphviz.org/">graphviz</a> to generate a
-graph showing the links between a set of pages in the wiki. Example usage:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!linkmap  pages=&quot;* and !blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Only links between mapped pages will be shown; links pointing to or from
-unmapped pages will be omitted. If the pages to include are not specified,
-the links between all pages (and other files) in the wiki are mapped. </p>
-
-<p>Here are descriptions of all the supported parameters to the <code>linkmap</code>
-directive:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>pages</code> - A <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> of the pages to map.</li>
-<li><code>height</code>, <code>width</code> - Limit the size of the map to a given height and width,
-in inches. Both must be specified for the limiting to take effect, otherwise
-the map&#39;s size is not limited.</li>
-<li><code>connected</code> - Controls whether to include pages on the map that link to
-no other pages (connected=no, the default), or to only show pages that
-link to others (connected=yes).</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>For best results, only a small set of pages should be mapped, since
-otherwise the map can become very large, unwieldy, and complicated.
-If too many pages are included, the map may get so large that graphviz
-cannot render it. Using the <code>connected</code> parameter is a good way to prune
-out pages that clutter the map.</p>
-
-</section>
-

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>listdirectives</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/listdirectives/">listdirectives</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive generates a list of available
-<a href="../">directives</a>.</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!listdirectives ]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>There is one optional keyword argument, <code>generated</code>.  Normally the
-<code>listdirectives</code> directive will list all built in directives and directives
-directly registered by plugins.  With this keyword, <code>listdirectives</code> will
-also list directives generated later.  For example, all <a href="../../../shortcuts/">shortcuts</a> are
-directives generated in turn by the <code>shortcut</code> directive.  They will only
-be listed if the <code>generated</code> argument is supplied.</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!listdirectives  generated]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>This extended list is often quite long, and often contains many
-undocumented directives.</p>
-
-</section>
-
-

-  placeholder="search" />
- </div>
-</form>

-</header>

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>map</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/map/">map</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive generates a hierarchical page map for the wiki. Example usage:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!map  pages=&quot;* and !blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>If the pages to include are not specified, all pages (and other files) in
-the wiki are mapped.</p>
-
-<p>By default, the names of pages are shown in the map. The <code>show</code> parameter
-can be used to show the titles or descriptions of pages instead (as set by
-the <a href="../meta/">meta</a> directive). For example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!map  pages=&quot;* and !blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot; show=title]]
-
-[[!map  pages=&quot;* and !blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot; show=description]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Hint: To limit the map to displaying pages less than a certain level deep,
-use a <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> like this: <code>pages=&quot;* and !*/*/*&quot;</code></p>
-
-</section>
-

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>meta</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/meta/">meta</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive allows inserting arbitrary metadata into the source of a page.
-Enter the metadata as follows:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!meta  field=&quot;value&quot;]]
-[[!meta  field=&quot;value&quot; param=&quot;value&quot; param=&quot;value&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The first form sets a given field to a given value, while the second form
-also specifies some additional sub-parameters. You can have only one field
-per <code>meta</code> directive, use more directives if you want to specify more fields.</p>
-
-<p>The field values are treated as HTML entity-escaped text, so you can include
-a quote in the text by writing <code>&amp;quot;</code> and so on.</p>
-
-<p>Supported fields:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><p>title</p>
-
-<p>Overrides the title of the page, which is generally the same as the
-page name.</p>
-
-<p>Note that if the title is overridden, a &quot;title_overridden&quot; variable will
-be set to a true value in the template; this can be used to format things
-differently in this case.</p>
-
-<p>An optional <code>sortas</code> parameter will be used preferentially when
-<a href="../../pagespec/sorting/">sorting</a> by <code>meta(title)</code>:</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  title=&quot;The Beatles&quot; sortas=&quot;Beatles, The&quot;]]</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  title=&quot;David Bowie&quot; sortas=&quot;Bowie, David&quot;]]</p></li>
-<li><p>license</p>
-
-<p>Specifies a license for the page, for example, &quot;GPL&quot;. Can contain
-WikiLinks and arbitrary markup.</p></li>
-<li><p>copyright</p>
-
-<p>Specifies the copyright of the page, for example, &quot;Copyright 2007 by
-Joey Hess&quot;. Can contain WikiLinks and arbitrary markup.</p></li>
-<li><p>author</p>
-
-<p>Specifies the author of a page.</p>
-
-<p>An optional <code>sortas</code> parameter will be used preferentially when
-<a href="../../pagespec/sorting/">sorting</a> by <code>meta(author)</code>:</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  author=&quot;Joey Hess&quot; sortas=&quot;Hess, Joey&quot;]]</p></li>
-<li><p>authorurl</p>
-
-<p>Specifies an url for the author of a page.</p></li>
-<li><p>description</p>
-
-<p>Specifies a short description for the page. This will be put in
-the html header, and can also be displayed by eg, the <a href="../map/">map</a> directive.</p></li>
-<li><p>permalink</p>
-
-<p>Specifies a permanent link to the page, if different than the page
-generated by ikiwiki.</p></li>
-<li><p>date</p>
-
-<p>Specifies the creation date of the page. The date can be entered in
-nearly any format, since it&#39;s parsed by <a href="http://search.cpan.org/search?mode=dist&amp;query=TimeDate">TimeDate</a>.</p></li>
-<li><p>stylesheet</p>
-
-<p>Adds a stylesheet to a page. The stylesheet is treated as a wiki link to
-a <code>.css</code> file in the wiki, so it cannot be used to add links to external
-stylesheets. Example:</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  stylesheet=somestyle rel=&quot;alternate stylesheet&quot;
-title=&quot;somestyle&quot;]]</p>
-
-<p>However, this will be scrubbed away if the 
-<a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/htmlscrubber/">htmlscrubber</a> plugin is enabled,
-since it can be used to insert unsafe content.</p></li>
-<li><p>script</p>
-
-<p>Adds a script to a page. The script is treated as a wiki link to
-a <code>.js</code> file in the wiki, so it cannot be used to add links to external
-scripts. The optional <code>defer</code> and <code>async</code> keywords can be used to set
-the corresponding HTML4 and HTML5 script options. Example:</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  script=somescript defer async]]</p>
-
-<p>The tag is subject to scrubbing as with the stylesheet and link fields.</p></li>
-<li><p>openid</p>
-
-<p>Adds html &lt;link&gt; tags to perform OpenID delegation to an external
-OpenID server. This lets you use an ikiwiki page as your OpenID.</p>
-
-<p>By default this will delegate for both <code>openid</code> and <code>openid2</code>. To only
-delegate for one, add a parameter such as <code>delegate=openid</code>.</p>
-
-<p>An optional <code>xrds-location</code>
-parameter lets you specify the location of any <a href="http://www.windley.com/archives/2007/05/using_xrds.shtml">eXtensible Resource
-DescriptorS</a>.</p>
-
-<p>Example:</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta openid=&quot;http://joeyh.myopenid.com/&quot;
-server=&quot;http://www.myopenid.com/server&quot;
-xrds-location=&quot;http://www.myopenid.com/xrds?username=joeyh.myopenid.com&quot;&quot;]]</p></li>
-<li><p>link</p>
-
-<p>Specifies a link to another page. This can be used as a way to make the
-wiki treat one page as linking to another without displaying a user-visible
-<a href="../../wikilink/">WikiLink</a>:</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  link=otherpage]]</p>
-
-<p>It can also be used to insert a html &lt;link&gt; tag. For example:</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  link=&quot;http://joeyh.myopenid.com/&quot; rel=&quot;openid.delegate&quot;]]</p>
-
-<p>However, this latter syntax won&#39;t be allowed if the 
-<a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/htmlscrubber/">htmlscrubber</a> plugin is enabled, since it can be used to
-insert unsafe content.</p></li>
-<li><p>redir</p>
-
-<p>Causes the page to redirect to another page in the wiki.</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  redir=otherpage]]</p>
-
-<p>Optionally, a delay (in seconds) can be specified. The default is to
-redirect without delay.</p>
-
-<p>It can also be used to redirect to an external url. For example:</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  redir=&quot;http://example.com/&quot;]]</p>
-
-<p>However, this latter syntax won&#39;t be allowed if the 
-<a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/htmlscrubber/">htmlscrubber</a> plugin is enabled, since it can be used to
-insert unsafe content.</p>
-
-<p>For both cases, an anchor to jump to inside the destination page may also be
-specified using the common <code>#ANCHOR</code> syntax.</p></li>
-<li><p>robots</p>
-
-<p>Causes the robots meta tag to be written:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!meta  robots=&quot;index, nofollow&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Valid values for the attribute are: &quot;index&quot;, &quot;noindex&quot;, &quot;follow&quot;, and
-&quot;nofollow&quot;. Multiple comma-separated values are allowed, but obviously only
-some combinations make sense. If there is no robots meta tag, &quot;index,
-follow&quot; is used as the default.</p>
-
-<p>The value is escaped, but its contents are not otherwise checked.</p></li>
-<li><p>guid</p>
-
-<p>Specifies a globally unique ID for a page. This guid should be a URI
-(in particular, it can be <code>urn:uuid:</code> followed by a UUID, as per
-<a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc4122.txt">RFC 4122</a>), and it will be used to identify the page&#39;s entry in RSS
-and Atom feeds. If not given, the default is to use the page&#39;s URL as its
-guid.</p>
-
-<p>This is mostly useful when a page has moved, to keep the guids for
-pages unchanged and avoid_flooding_aggregators
-(see <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/tips/howto_avoid_flooding_aggregators/">tips/howto avoid flooding aggregators</a>).</p></li>
-<li><p>updated</p>
-
-<p>Specifies a fake modification time for a page, to be output into RSS and
-Atom feeds. This is useful to avoid flooding aggregators that sort by
-modification time, like Planet: for instance, when editing an old blog post
-to add tags, you could set <code>updated</code> to be one second later than the original
-value. The date/time can be given in any format that
-<a href="http://search.cpan.org/search?mode=dist&amp;query=TimeDate">TimeDate</a> can understand, just like the <code>date</code> field.</p></li>
-<li><p>foaf</p>
-
-<p>Adds a Friend of a Friend (<a href="http://wiki.foaf-project.org/w/Autodiscovery">FOAF</a>)
-reference to a page.</p>
-
-<p>Example:</p>
-
-<p>[[!meta  foaf=foaf.rdf]]</p></li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>If the field is not one of the above predefined fields, the metadata will be
-written to the generated html page as a &lt;meta&gt; header. However, this
-won&#39;t be allowed if the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/htmlscrubber/">htmlscrubber</a> plugin is enabled,
-since it can be used to insert unsafe content.</p>
-
-</section>
-

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>more</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/more/">more</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive provides a way to have a &quot;more&quot; link on a post in a blog, that
-leads to the full version of the page. Use it like this:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!more  linktext=&quot;click for more&quot; text=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-This is the rest of my post. Not intended for people catching up on
-their blogs at 30,000 feet. Because I like to make things
-difficult.
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>If the <code>linktext</code> parameter is omitted it defaults to just &quot;more&quot;.</p>
-
-<p>An optional <code>pages</code> parameter can be used to specify a
-<a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a>, and then the &quot;more&quot; link will only be displayed
-when the page is inlined into a page matching that PageSpec, and otherwise
-the full content shown.</p>
-
-<p>Note that you can accomplish something similar using a <a href="../toggle/">toggle</a> instead.</p>
-
-</section>
-

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>orphans</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/orphans/">orphans</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive generates a list of possibly orphaned pages -- pages that no
-other page links to. Example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!orphans  pages=&quot;* and !blog/*&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The optional parameter &quot;pages&quot; can be a <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> specifying the
-pages to check for orphans, default is search them all.</p>
-
-<p>Note that it takes backlinks into account, but does not count inlining a
-page as linking to it, so will generally count many blog-type pages as
-orphans.</p>
-
-</section>
-
-
-

-</code></pre>
-

-<form method="get" action="http://www.google.com/search" id="searchform">
- <div>
-  <input name="sitesearch" value="http://weakish.github.com/" type="hidden" />
-  <input name="q" value="" id="searchbox" size="16" maxlength="255" type="text"
-  placeholder="search" />
- </div>
-</form>

-</header>

-
-
-</section>

-<div id="pagebody">
-
-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>pagestats</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/pagestats/">pagestats</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive can generate stats about how pages link to each other. It can
-produce either a tag cloud, or a table counting the number of links to each
-page.</p>
-
-<p>Here&#39;s how to use it to create a <a href="../tag/">tag</a> cloud, with tags sized based
-on frequency of use:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!pagestats  pages=&quot;tags/*&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Here&#39;s how to create a list of tags, sized by use as they would be in a
-cloud.</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!pagestats  style=&quot;list&quot; pages=&quot;tags/*&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>And here&#39;s how to create a table of all the pages on the wiki:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!pagestats  style=&quot;table&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The optional <code>among</code> parameter limits the pages whose outgoing links are
-considered. For instance, to display a cloud of tags used on blog
-entries, while ignoring other pages that use those tags, you could use:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!pagestats  pages=&quot;tags/*&quot; among=&quot;blog/posts/*&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Or to display a cloud of tags related to Linux, you could use:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!pagestats  pages=&quot;tags/* and !tags/linux&quot; among=&quot;tagged(linux)&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The optional <code>show</code> parameter limits display to the specified number of
-pages. For instance, to show a table of the top ten pages with the most
-links:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!pagestats  style=&quot;table&quot; show=&quot;10&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The optional <code>class</code> parameter can be used to control the class
-of the generated tag cloud <code>div</code> or page stats <code>table</code>.</p>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-
-</div>

-
-<p>This directive allows a page to be displayed using a different
-<a href="../../../templates/">template</a> than the default <code>page.tmpl</code> template.</p>
-
-<p>The page text is inserted into the template, so the template controls the
-overall look and feel of the wiki page. This is in contrast to the
-<a href="../template/">template</a> directive, which allows inserting templates
-<em>into</em> the body of a page.</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!pagetemplate  template=&quot;my_fancy.tmpl&quot;]]
-</code></pre>

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>ping</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/pinger/">pinger</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive allows ikiwiki to be configured to hit a URL each time it
-updates the wiki. One way to use this is in conjunction with the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/pingee/">pingee</a>
-plugin to set up a loosely coupled mirror network, or a branched version of
-a wiki. By pinging the mirror or branch each time the main wiki changes, it
-can be kept up-to-date.</p>
-
-<pre><code>    [[!ping  from=&quot;http://mywiki.com/&quot;
-    to=&quot;http://otherwiki.com/ikiwiki.cgi?do=ping&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The &quot;from&quot; parameter must be identical to the url of the wiki that is doing
-the pinging. This is used to prevent ping loops.</p>
-
-<p>The &quot;to&quot; parameter is the url to ping. The example shows how to ping
-another ikiwiki instance.</p>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>poll</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/poll/">poll</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive allows you to create online polls in the wiki. Here&#39;s an
-example use:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!poll  0 &quot;red&quot; 0 &quot;green&quot; 0 &quot;blue&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The numbers indicate how many users voted for that choice. When a user
-votes for a choice in the poll, the page is modified and the number
-incremented.</p>
-
-<p>While some basic precautions are taken to prevent users from accidentially
-voting twice, this sort of poll should not be counted on to be very
-accurate; all the usual concerns about web based polling apply. Unless the
-page that the poll is in is locked, users can even edit the page and change
-the numbers!</p>
-
-<p>Parameters: </p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>open</code> - Whether voting is still open. Set to &quot;no&quot; to close the poll to
-voting.</li>
-<li><code>total</code> - Show total number of votes at bottom of poll. Default is &quot;yes&quot;.</li>
-<li><code>percent</code> - Whether to display percents. Default is &quot;yes&quot;.</li>
-</ul>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-
-</div>

diff --git a/ikiwiki/directive/postsparkline/index.html b/ikiwiki/directive/postsparkline/index.html
@@ -1,146 +0,0 @@
-<!DOCTYPE html>
-<html>
-
-<head>

-<title>postsparkline</title>
-
-<link rel="icon" href="../../../favicon.ico" type="image/x-icon" />

-<link rel="stylesheet" href="../../../local.css" type="text/css" />

-<body>

-<article class="page">

-<section class="pageheader">
-<header class="header">

-</span>
-</span>
-
-
-<form method="get" action="http://www.google.com/search" id="searchform">
- <div>
-  <input name="sitesearch" value="http://weakish.github.com/" type="hidden" />
-  <input name="q" value="" id="searchbox" size="16" maxlength="255" type="text"
-  placeholder="search" />
- </div>

-<div id="pagebody">
-
-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>postsparkline</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/postsparkline/">postsparkline</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive uses the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/sparkline/">sparkline</a> plugin to create a
-<a href="../sparkline/">sparkline</a> of statistics about a set of pages, such as posts to a blog.</p>
-
-<h1>examples</h1>
-
-<pre><code>Post interval: 
-[[!postsparkline  pages=&quot;blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot; max=100
-formula=interval style=bar barwidth=2 barspacing=1 height=13]]
-
-Posts per month this year: 
-[[!postsparkline  pages=&quot;blog/* and !*/Discussion&quot; max=12
-formula=permonth style=bar barwidth=2 barspacing=1 height=13]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<h1>usage</h1>
-
-<p>All options aside from the <code>pages</code>, <code>max</code>, <code>formula</code>, <code>time</code>, and <code>color</code>
-options are the same as in <a href="../sparkline/">sparkline</a> directive.</p>
-
-<p>You don&#39;t need to specify any data points (though you can if you want to).
-Instead, data points are automatically generated based on the creation
-times of pages matched by the specified <code>pages</code> <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a>. A
-maximum of <code>max</code> data points will be generated.</p>
-
-<p>The <code>formula</code> parameter controls the formula used to generate data points.
-Available formulae:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>interval</code> - The height of each point represents how long it has been
-since the previous post.</li>
-<li><code>perday</code> - Each point represents a day; the height represents how
-many posts were made that day.</li>
-<li><code>permonth</code> - Each point represents a month; the height represents how
-many posts were made that month.</li>
-<li><code>peryear</code> - Each point represents a year; the height represents how
-many posts were made that year.</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>The <code>time</code> parameter has a default value of &quot;ctime&quot;, since formulae use
-the creation times of pages by default. If you instead want
-them to use the modification times of pages, set it to &quot;mtime&quot;.</p>
-
-<p>To change the color used to draw the sparkline, use the <code>color</code> parameter.
-For example, &quot;color=red&quot;.</p>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-
-</div>
-

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>progress</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/progress/">progress</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive generates a progress bar.</p>
-
-<p>There are two possible parameter sets.  The first is a single parameter
-&quot;percent&quot; which holds a percentage figure of how complete the progress bar is.</p>
-
-<p>The second possible set of parameters is a pair of <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a>s,
-<code>totalpages</code> and <code>donepages</code>. The directive counts the number of
-pages in each pagespec and shows the percentage of the total pages that are
-done.</p>
-
-<p>For example, to show what percentage of pages have
-discussion pages:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!progress  totalpages=&quot;* and !*/Discussion&quot; donepages=&quot;*/Discussion&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-</section>

-<p>The <code>sidebar</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/sidebar/">sidebar</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive can specify a custom sidebar to display on the page,
-overriding any sidebar that is displayed globally.</p>
-
-<p>If no custom sidebar content is specified, it forces the sidebar page to
-be used as the sidebar, even if the <code>global_sidebars</code> setting has been
-used to disable use of the sidebar page by default.</p>
-
-<h2>examples</h2>
-
-<pre><code>[[!sidebar  content=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-This is my custom sidebar for this page.
-
-\[[!calendar pages=&quot;posts/*&quot;]]
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-
-[[!sidebar ]]
-</code></pre>

-<form method="get" action="http://www.google.com/search" id="searchform">
- <div>
-  <input name="sitesearch" value="http://weakish.github.com/" type="hidden" />
-  <input name="q" value="" id="searchbox" size="16" maxlength="255" type="text"

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>sparkline</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/sparkline/">sparkline</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive allows for embedding sparklines into wiki pages. A
-sparkline is a small word-size graphic chart, that is designed to be
-displayed alongside text.</p>
-
-<h1>examples</h1>
-
-<pre><code>[[!sparkline  1 3 5 -3 10 0 width=40 height=16
-featurepoint=&quot;4,-3,red,3&quot; featurepoint=&quot;5,10,green,3&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>This creates a simple line graph, graphing several points.
-It will be drawn 40 pixels wide and 16 pixels high. The high point in the
-line has a green marker, and the low point has a red marker.</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!sparkline  1 -1(red) 1 -1(red) 1 1 1 -1(red) -1(red) style=bar barwidth=2
-barspacing=1 height=13]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>This more complex example generates a bar graph. 
-The bars are 2 pixels wide, and separated by one pixel, and the graph is 13
-pixels tall. Width is determined automatically for bar graphs. The points
-with negative values are colored red, instead of the default black.</p>
-
-<h1>usage</h1>
-
-<p>The form for the data points is &quot;x,y&quot;, or just &quot;y&quot; if the x values don&#39;t
-matter. Bar graphs can also add &quot;(color)&quot; to specify a color for that bar.</p>
-
-<p>The following named parameters are recognised. Most of these are the same
-as those used by the underlying sparkline library, which is documented in
-more detail in <a href="http://sparkline.wikispaces.com/usage">its wiki</a>.</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>style</code> - Either &quot;line&quot; (the default) or &quot;bar&quot;.</li>
-<li><code>width</code> - Width of the graph in pixels. Only needed for line graphs.</li>
-<li><code>height</code> - Height of the graph in pixels. Defaults to 16.</li>
-<li><code>barwidth</code> - Width of bars in a bar graph. Default is 1 pixel.</li>
-<li><code>barspacing</code> - Spacing between bars in a bar graph, in pixels. Default is
-1 pixel.</li>
-<li><code>ymin</code>, <code>ymax</code> - Minimum and maximum values for the Y axis. This is
-normally calculated automatically, but can be explicitly specified to get
-the same values for multiple related graphs.</li>
-<li><p><code>featurepoint</code> - Adds a circular marker to a line graph, with optional
-text. This can be used to label significant points.</p>
-
-<p>The value is a comma-delimited list of parameters specifying the feature
-point: X value, Y value, color name, circle diameter, text (optional),
-and text location (optional). Example: <code>featurepoint=&quot;3,5,blue,3&quot;</code></p>
-
-<p>Available values for the text location are: &quot;top&quot;, &quot;right&quot;, &quot;bottom&quot;, and
-&quot;left&quot;.</p></li>
-</ul>
-
-</section>
-

-<form method="get" action="http://www.google.com/search" id="searchform">
- <div>
-  <input name="sitesearch" value="http://weakish.github.com/" type="hidden" />
-  <input name="q" value="" id="searchbox" size="16" maxlength="255" type="text"
-  placeholder="search" />

-<div id="pagebody">
-
-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>table</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/table/">table</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive can build HTML tables from data in CSV (comma-separated values)
-or DSV (delimiter-separated values) format.</p>
-
-<h2>examples</h2>
-
-<pre><code>[[!table  data=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-Customer |Amount
-Fulanito |134,34
-Menganito|234,56
-Menganito|234,56
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-
-[[!table  class=&quot;book_record&quot; format=csv file=&quot;data/books/record1&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>In this second example the <code>record1</code> page should be similar to:</p>
-
-<pre><code>&quot;Title&quot;,&quot;Perl Best Practices&quot;
-&quot;Author&quot;,&quot;Damian Conway&quot;
-&quot;Publisher&quot;,&quot;O&rsquo;Reilly&quot;
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>To make a cell span multiple columns, follow it with one or more empty
-cells. For example:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!table  data=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-left||right|
-a|b|c|d
-this cell spans 4 columns|||
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<h2>usage</h2>
-
-<ul>
-<li><code>data</code> - Values for the table.</li>
-<li><code>file</code> - A file in the wiki containing the data.</li>
-<li><code>format</code> - The format of the data, either &quot;csv&quot;, &quot;dsv&quot;, or &quot;auto&quot;
-(the default).</li>
-<li><code>delimiter</code> - The character used to separate fields. By default,
-DSV format uses a pipe (<code>|</code>), and CSV uses a comma (<code>,</code>).</li>
-<li><code>class</code> - A CSS class for the table html element.</li>
-<li><code>header</code> - By default, or if set to &quot;row&quot;, the first data line is used
-as the table header. Set it to &quot;no&quot; to make a table without a header, or
-&quot;column&quot; to make the first column be the header.</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>For tab-delimited tables (often obtained by copying and pasting from HTML
-or a spreadsheet), <code>delimiter</code> must be set to a literal tab character. These
-are difficult to type in most web browsers - copying and pasting one from
-the table data is likely to be the easiest way.</p>
-
-</section>
-

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>tag</code> and <code>taglink</code> directives are supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/tag/">tag</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>These directives allow tagging pages. List tags as follows:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!tag  tech life linux]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The tags work the same as if you had put a (hidden) <a href="../../wikilink/">WikiLink</a> on
-the page for each tag, so you can use a <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> match all
-pages that are tagged with a given tag, for example. The tags will also
-show up on blog entries and at the bottom of the tagged pages, as well as
-in RSS and Atom feeds.</p>
-
-<p>If you want a visible <a href="../../wikilink/">WikiLink</a> along with the tag, use taglink
-instead:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!taglink  foo]]
-[[!taglink  tagged_as_foo|foo]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Note that if the wiki is configured to use a tagbase, then the tags will be
-located under a base directory, such as &quot;tags/&quot;. This is a useful way to
-avoid having to write the full path to tags, if you want to keep them
-grouped together out of the way. Also, since ikiwiki then knows where to put
-tags, it will automatically create tag pages when new tags are used.</p>
-
-<p>Bear in mind that specifying a tagbase means you will need to incorporate it
-into the <code>link()</code> <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> you use: e.g., if your tagbase is
-<code>tag</code>, you would match pages tagged &quot;foo&quot; with <code>link(tag/foo)</code>.</p>
-
-<p>If you want to override the tagbase for a particular tag, you can use
-something like this:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!tag  /foo]]
-[[!taglink  /foo]]
-</code></pre>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-
-</div>

-<form method="get" action="http://www.google.com/search" id="searchform">

-<div id="pagebody">
-
-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>template</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/template/">template</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>The template directive allows wiki pages to be used as templates.
-These templates can be filled out and inserted into other pages in the
-wiki using the directive. The <a href="../../../templates/">templates</a> page lists templates
-that can be used with this directive.</p>
-
-<p>The directive has an <code>id</code> parameter
-that identifies the template to use. The remaining parameters are used to
-fill out the template.</p>
-
-<h2>Example</h2>
-
-<pre><code>[[!template  id=note text=&quot;&quot;&quot;Here is the text to insert into my note.&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>This fills out the <code>note</code> template, filling in the <code>text</code> field with
-the specified value, and inserts the result into the page.</p>
-
-<h2>Using a template</h2>
-
-<p>Generally, a value can include any markup that would be allowed in the wiki
-page outside the template. Triple-quoting the value even allows quotes to
-be included in it. Combined with multi-line quoted values, this allows for
-large chunks of marked up text to be embedded into a template:</p>
-
-<pre><code>    [[!template  id=foo name=&quot;Sally&quot; color=&quot;green&quot; age=8 notes=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-    * [[Charley]]&#39;s sister.
-    * &quot;I want to be an astronaut when I grow up.&quot;
-    * Really 8 and a half.
-    &quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<h2>Creating a template</h2>
-
-<p>The template is a regular wiki page, located in the <code>templates/</code>
-subdirectory inside the source directory of the wiki.</p>
-
-<p>Alternatively, templates can be stored in a directory outside the wiki,
-as files with the extension &quot;.tmpl&quot;.
-By default, these are searched for in <code>/usr/share/ikiwiki/templates</code>,
-the <code>templatedir</code> setting can be used to make another directory be searched
-first.  When referring to templates outside the wiki source directory, the &quot;id&quot;
-parameter is not interpreted as a pagespec, and you must include the full filename
-of the template page, including the &quot;.tmpl&quot; extension. E.g.:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!template  id=blogpost.tmpl]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The template uses the syntax used by the <a href="http://search.cpan.org/search?mode=dist&amp;query=HTML%3A%3ATemplate">HTML::Template</a> perl
-module, which allows for some fairly complex things to be done. Consult its
-documentation for the full syntax, but all you really need to know are a
-few things:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li>Each parameter you pass to the template directive will generate a 
-template variable. There are also some pre-defined variables like PAGE
-and BASENAME.</li>
-<li>To insert the value of a variable, use <code>&lt;TMPL_VAR variable&gt;</code>. Wiki markup
-in the value will first be converted to html.</li>
-<li>To insert the raw value of a variable, with wiki markup not yet converted
-to html, use <code>&lt;TMPL_VAR raw_variable&gt;</code>.</li>
-<li>To make a block of text conditional on a variable being set use
-<code>&lt;TMPL_IF variable&gt;text&lt;/TMPL_IF&gt;</code>.</li>
-<li>To use one block of text if a variable is set and a second if it&#39;s not,
-use <code>&lt;TMPL_IF variable&gt;text&lt;TMPL_ELSE&gt;other text&lt;/TMPL_IF&gt;</code></li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>Here&#39;s a sample template:</p>
-
-<pre><code>    &lt;span class=&quot;infobox&quot;&gt;
-    Name: [[&lt;TMPL_VAR raw_name&gt;]]&lt;br /&gt;
-    Age: &lt;TMPL_VAR age&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
-    &lt;TMPL_IF color&gt;
-    Favorite color: &lt;TMPL_VAR color&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
-    &lt;TMPL_ELSE&gt;
-    No favorite color.&lt;br /&gt;
-    &lt;/TMPL_IF&gt;
-    &lt;TMPL_IF notes&gt;
-    &lt;hr /&gt;
-    &lt;TMPL_VAR notes&gt;
-    &lt;/TMPL_IF&gt;
-    &lt;/span&gt;
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The filled out template will be formatted the same as the rest of the page
-that contains it, so you can include WikiLinks and all other forms of wiki
-markup in the template. Note though that such WikiLinks will not show up as
-backlinks to the page that uses the template.</p>
-
-<p>Note the use of &quot;raw_name&quot; inside the <a href="../../wikilink/">WikiLink</a> generator in the
-example above. This ensures that if the name contains something that might
-be mistaken for wiki markup, it&#39;s not converted to html before being
-processed as a <a href="../../wikilink/">WikiLink</a>.</p>
-
-</section>
-
-

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>testpagespec</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/testpagespec/">testpagespec</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive allows testing a <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> to see if it matches a
-page, and to see the part that matches, or causes the match to fail.</p>
-
-<p>Example uses:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!testpagespec  pagespec=&quot;foopage and barpage&quot; match=&quot;foopage&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>This will print out something like &quot;no match: barpage does not match
-foopage&quot;, highlighting which part of the <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> is causing
-the match to fail.</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!testpagespec  pagespec=&quot;foopage or !bar*&quot; match=&quot;barpage&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>This will print out something like &quot;no match: bar* matches barpage&quot;, since
-the part of the <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> that fails is this negated match.</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!testpagespec  pagespec=&quot;foopage or barpage&quot; match=&quot;barpage&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>This will print out something like &quot;match: barpage matches barpage&quot;,
-indicating the part of the <a href="../../pagespec/">PageSpec</a> that caused it to match.</p>
-
-</section>
-

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>teximg</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/teximg/">teximg</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive renders LaTeX formulas into images.</p>
-
-<h2>examples</h2>
-
-<pre><code>[[!teximg  code=&quot;\frac{1}{2}&quot;]]
-[[!teximg  code=&quot;E = - \frac{Z^2 \cdot  \mu \cdot e^4}{32\pi^2 \epsilon_0^2 \hbar^2 n^2}&quot; ]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>To scale the image, use height=x:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!teximg  code=&quot;\frac{1}{2}&quot; height=&quot;17&quot;]]
-[[!teximg  code=&quot;\frac{1}{2}&quot; height=&quot;8&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>If no height is chosen the default height 12 is used. Valid heights are: 8, 9,
-10, 11, 12, 14, 17, 20. If another height is entered, the closest available
-height is used.</p>
-
-<p>To add an alt text to the image, use alt=&quot;text&quot;:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!teximg  code=&quot;\frac{1}{2}&quot; alt=&quot;1/2&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>toc</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/toc/">toc</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>Add a table of contents to a page:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!toc  ]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The table of contents will be automatically generated based on the
-headers of the page. By default only the largest headers present on the
-page will be shown; to control how many levels of headers are shown, use
-the <code>levels</code> parameter:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!toc  levels=2]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The toc directive will take the level of the first header as the topmost
-level, even if there are higher levels seen later in the file.</p>
-
-<p>To create a table of contents that only shows headers starting with a given
-level, use the <code>startlevel</code> parameter. For example, to show only h2 and
-smaller headers:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!toc  startlevel=2]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>The table of contents will be created as an ordered list. If you want
-an unordered list instead, you can change the list-style in your local
-style sheet.</p>
-
-</section>
-

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>The <code>toggle</code> and <code>toggleable</code> directives are supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/toggle/">toggle</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>With these directives you can create links on pages that, when clicked, toggle
-display of other parts of the page.</p>
-
-<p>It uses javascript to accomplish this; browsers without javascript will
-always see the full page content.</p>
-
-<p>Example use:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!toggle  id=&quot;ipsum&quot; text=&quot;show&quot;]]
-
-[[!toggleable  id=&quot;ipsum&quot; text=&quot;&quot;&quot;
-Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet, consectetur adipisicing elit, sed do
-eiusmod tempor incididunt ut labore et dolore magna aliqua. Ut enim
-ad minim veniam, quis nostrud exercitation ullamco laboris nisi ut
-aliquip ex ea commodo consequat.
-
-[[!toggle id=&quot;ipsum&quot; text=&quot;hide&quot;]]
-&quot;&quot;&quot;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>Note that you can include wiki markup in the toggleable text,
-including even additional toggles, as shown in the above example.</p>
-
-<p>Also, the toggle and the togglable definitions do not need to be next to
-each other, but can be located anywhere on the page. There can also be
-mutiple toggles that all toggle a single togglable.</p>
-
-<p>The id has a default value of &quot;default&quot;, so can be omitted in simple cases.</p>
-
-<p>If you&#39;d like a toggleable to be displayed by default, and toggle to
-hidden, then pass a parameter &quot;open=yes&quot; when setting up the toggleable.</p>
-
-</section>
-
-
-
-
-
-</div>

-<p>The <code>version</code> directive is supplied by the <a href="http://ikiwiki.info/plugins/version/">version</a> plugin.</p>
-
-<p>This directive allows inserting the version of ikiwiki onto a page.</p>
-
-<p>Whenever ikiwiki is upgraded to a new version, the page will be rebuilt,
-updating the version number.</p>
-
-<p>Use is simple:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!version  ]]
-</code></pre>

-<article class="page">
-
-<section class="pageheader">
-<header class="header">
-<span>
-<span class="parentlinks">

-<a href="../../">weakish</a>/ 
-
-<a href="../">ikiwiki</a>/ 
-
-</span>
-<span class="title">
-Formatting wiki pages
-
-</span>
-</span>
-
-
-<form method="get" action="http://www.google.com/search" id="searchform">
- <div>
-  <input name="sitesearch" value="http://weakish.github.com/" type="hidden" />
-  <input name="q" value="" id="searchbox" size="16" maxlength="255" type="text"
-  placeholder="search" />
- </div>

-</header>

-</section>

-<div id="pagebody">
-
-<section id="content">
-<p>Text on this wiki is, by default, written in a form very close to how you
-might write text for an email message. This style of text formatting is
-called <a href="../markdown/">MarkDown</a>, and it works like this:</p>
-
-<p>Leave blank lines between paragraphs.</p>
-
-<p>You can <em>*emphasise*</em> or <strong>**strongly emphasise**</strong> text by placing it
-in single or double asterisks.</p>
-
-<p>To create a list, start each line with an asterisk:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li>&quot;* this is my list&quot;</li>
-<li>&quot;* another item&quot;</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>To make a numbered list, start each line with a number (any number will
-do) followed by a period:</p>
-
-<ol>
-<li>&quot;1. first line&quot;</li>
-<li>&quot;2. second line&quot;</li>
-<li>&quot;2. third line&quot;</li>
-</ol>
-
-<p>To create a header, start a line with one or more <code>#</code> characters followed
-by a space and the header text. The number of <code>#</code> characters controls the
-size of the header:</p>
-
-<h1># h1</h1>
-
-<h2>## h2</h2>
-
-<h3>### h3</h3>
-
-<h4>#### h4</h4>
-
-<h5>##### h5</h5>
-
-<h6>###### h6</h6>
-
-<p>To create a horizontal rule, just write three or more dashes or stars on
-their own line:</p>
-
-<hr />
-
-<p>To quote someone, prefix the quote with &quot;&gt;&quot;:</p>
-
-<blockquote>
-  <p>To be or not to be,
-  that is the question.</p>
-</blockquote>
-
-<p>To write a code block, indent each line with a tab or 4 spaces:</p>
-
-<pre><code>10 PRINT &quot;Hello, world!&quot;
-20 GOTO 10
-</code></pre>
-
-<p>To link to an url or email address, you can just put the
-url in angle brackets: &lt;<a href="http://ikiwiki.info">http://ikiwiki.info</a>&gt;, or you can use the
-form [link text](url)</p>
-
-<hr />
-
-<p>In addition to basic html formatting using <a href="../markdown/">MarkDown</a>, this wiki lets
-you use the following additional features:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li><p>To link to another page on the wiki, place the page&#39;s name inside double
-square brackets. So you would use <code>[[WikiLink]]</code> to link to <a href="../wikilink/">WikiLink</a>.</p></li>
-<li><p>Use <a href="../../shortcuts/">shortcuts</a> to link to common resources.</p>
-
-<p>[[!wikipedia  War_of_1812]]</p></li>
-<li><p>Create and fill out <a href="../../templates/">templates</a> for repeated chunks of
-parameterized wiki text.</p></li>
-<li><p>Insert various <a href="../directive/">directives</a> onto a page to perform useful
-actions.
-For example, you can:</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li>Add a table of contents to a page:</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>[[!toc ]]</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li>Change the title of a page:</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>[[!meta  title=&quot;full page title&quot;]]</p>
-
-<ul>
-<li>Create a blog by inlining a set of pages:</li>
-</ul>
-
-<p>[[!inline  pages=&quot;blog/*&quot;]]</p>
-
-<p>Full list of <a href="../directive/">directives</a> enabled for this wiki:</p></li>
-</ul>
-
-<ul class="listdirectives"><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/brokenlinks/">brokenlinks</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/format/">format</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/if/">if</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/inline/">inline</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/linkmap/">linkmap</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/listdirectives/">listdirectives</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/map/">map</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/meta/">meta</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/orphans/">orphans</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/pagestats/">pagestats</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/pagetemplate/">pagetemplate</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/shortcut/">shortcut</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/table/">table</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/tag/">tag</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/taglink/">taglink</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/template/">template</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/teximg/">teximg</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/toc/">toc</a></li><li class="listdirectives"><a href="../directive/version/">version</a></li></ul>
-
-</section>
-
-

-<section id="content">
-<p><a href="http://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/">Markdown</a>
-is a minimal markup language that resembles plain text as used in
-email messages. It is the markup language used by this wiki by default.</p>
-
-<p>For documentation about the markdown syntax, see <a href="../formatting/">formatting</a> and
-<a href="http://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/syntax">Markdown: syntax</a>.</p>
-
-<p>Note that <a href="../wikilink/">WikiLinks</a> and <a href="../directive/">directives</a> are not part
-of the markdown syntax, and are the only bit of markup that this wiki
-handles internally.</p>
-
-</section>

-<div id="pagebody">

-<section id="content">
-<p>This wiki has OpenID <strong>enabled</strong>.</p>
-
-<p><a href="http://openid.net">OpenID</a> is a decentralized authentication mechanism
-that allows you to have one login that you can use on a growing number of
-websites.</p>
-
-<p>If you have an account with some of the larger web service providers,
-you might already have an OpenID. 
-<a href="http://openiddirectory.com/openid-providers-c-1.html">Directory of OpenID providers</a></p>
-
-<p>To sign in to this wiki using OpenID, just enter it in the OpenID field in the
-signin form. You do not need to give this wiki a password or go through any
-registration process when using OpenID.</p>
-
-<hr />
-
-<p>It&#39;s also possible to make a page in the wiki usable as an OpenID url,
-by delegating it to an openid server. Here&#39;s an example of how to do that:</p>
-
-<pre><code>[[!meta  openid=&#34;http://yourid.myopenid.com/&#34;
-       server=&#34;http://www.myopenid.com/server&#34;]]
-</code></pre>
-
-</section>
-
